1 Scope 1 
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN Alliance. 2 
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN and may change following formal 3 
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN Alliance modify the contents of the present document, it will be re-released by O-4 
RAN with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows:  5 
Release x.y.z 6 
where: 7 
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, 8 
etc. (the initial approved document will have x=01). 9 
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document.  10 
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the 11 
editing process. 12 
The present document specifies the E2 Service Model (E2SM) for the Near RT RIC RAN Control interaction.  13

3 Definitions and Abbreviations 1 
3.1 Definitions 2 
E2 Node: as defined in E2GAP [2].  3 
RAN Function: as defined in E2GAP [2] 4 
E2 Service Model: The description of the Services exposed by a specific RAN function within an E2 node over the E2 5 
interface towards the Near-RT RIC. 6 
SpCell: as defined in TS 37.340 [31]. 7 
3.2 Abbreviations 8 
For the purposes of the present document, the following abbreviations apply.  9 
O-CU  O- RAN Central Unit 10 
O-CU-CP O- RAN Central Unit – Control Plane 11 
O-CU-UP O- RAN Central Unit – User Plane 12 
O-DU O- RAN Distributed Unit   13 
Near-RT RIC Near-real-time RAN Intelligent Controller 14 
RC RAN Control 15

4 General 1 
4.1 Procedure Specification Principles 2 
The principle for specifying the procedure logic is to specify the functional behaviour of the terminating node  exactly 3 
and completely. Any rule that specifies the behaviour of the originating node shall be possible to be verified with 4 
information that is visible within the system. 5 
The following specification principles have been applied for the procedure text in c lause 8: 6 
- The procedure text discriminates between: 7 
1) Functionality which "shall" be executed. 8 
 The procedure text indicates that the receiving node "shall" perform a certain function Y under a certain 9 
condition. If the receiving node supports procedure X but cannot perform functionality Y requested in the 10 
REQUEST message of a Class 1 EP, the receiving node shall respond with the message used to report 11 
unsuccessful outcome for this procedure, containing an appropriate cause value.  12 
2) Functionality which "shall, if supported" be executed. 13 
 The procedure text indicates that the receiving node "shall, if supported," perform a certain function Y under 14 
a certain condition. If the receiving node supports procedure X, but does not support functionality Y, the 15 
receiving node shall proceed with the execution of the EP, possibly informing the requesting node about the 16 
not supported functionality. 17 
- Any required inclusion of an optional IE in a response message is explicitly indicated in the procedure text. If the 18 
procedure text does not explicitly indicate that an optional IE shall be included in a response message, the 19 
optional IE shall not be included. For requirements on including Criticality Diagnostics IE, see clause 10. 20 
4.2 Forwards and Backwards Compatibility 21 
The forwards and backwards compatibility of the protocol is assured by a mechanism where all current and future 22 
messages, and IEs or groups of related IEs, include ID and criticality fields that are coded in a standard format that will 23 
not be changed in the future. These parts can always be decoded regardless of the standard version. 24 
4.3 Specification Notations 25 
For the purposes of the present document, the following notations apply: 26 
Service when referring to a Service in the specification the SERVICE NAME is written with upper case 27 
characters and in bold followed by the word "service", e.g. REPORT service. 28 
Procedure When referring to an elementary procedure in the specification the Procedure Name is written with 29 
the first letters in each word in upper case characters followed by the word "procedure", e.g. 30 
Handover Preparation procedure. 31 
Message When referring to a message in the specification the MESSAGE NAME is written with all letters 32 
in upper case characters followed by the word "message", e.g. HANDOVER REQUEST message.  33 
IE When referring to an information element (IE) in the specification the Information Element Name  34 
is written with the first letters in each word in upper case characters and all letters in Italic font 35 
followed by the abbreviation "IE", e.g. E-RAB ID IE. 36 
Value of an IE When referring to the value of an information element (IE) in the specification the "Value" is 37 
written as it is specified in the specification enclosed by quotation marks, e.g. "Value".  38

4.4 Identifiers 1 
For the purposes of the present document, the following identifiers are defined:  2 
Style Type The identifier used to nominate a specific approach or Style used to exposing a given RIC Service 3 
(REPORT, INSERT, CONTROL and POLICY).  The same E2SM may support more than one 4 
Style for each RIC Service. 5 
Format Type The identifier used to nominate a specific formatting approach used to encode one of the E2AP IEs 6 
defined in this E2SM.  The same E2SM may support more than one encoding Formats for each 7 
E2AP IE and each E2AP IE message encoding Format may be used by one or more RIC Service 8 
Styles. 9

6 RAN Function Service Model Description 1 
6.1 RAN Function Overview 2 
For the purposes of this E2 Service Model, E2SM-RC, the E2 Node terminating the E2 Interface is assumed to host one 3 
or more instances of the RAN Function “RAN Control” which performs the following functionalities: 4 
- E2 REPORT services used to expose RAN control and UE context related information  5 
- E2 INSERT services used to suspend RAN control related call processes 6 
- E2 CONTROL services used to resume or initiate RAN control related call processes, modify RAN 7 
configuration and/or E2 service-related UE context information 8 
- E2 POLICY services used to modify the behaviour of RAN control related processes  9 
This E2SM specification provides a set of RAN Function exposure services described in clause 6.2 and has been 10 
prepared with the assumption that the same E2SM may be used to describe either a single RAN Function in the E2 11 
Node handling all RAN control related call processes or more than one RAN Function in the E2 Node with each 12 
instance handling a subset of the RAN control related call processes on the E2 Node.  13 
6.2 RAN Function exposure services 14 
6.2.1 REPORT service 15 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following REPORT  services: 16 
- Copy of Complete message (from Network Interface or RRC), used for monitoring POLICY services, data 17 
gathering (to populate the Near-RT RIC UE-NIB and/or ML services data pipeline), etc. 18 
- Call process outcome with associated information on UE context and/or RAN status information, used for 19 
monitoring [CONTROL and] POLICY services, data gathering (to populate the Near -RT RIC UE-NIB and/or 20 
ML services data pipeline), etc.  21 
- E2 Node Information and Cell related Information, used for monitoring of E2 Node and Cell configuration 22 
changes, triggering POLICY deletion, changing notifications (to reset Near-RT RIC optimization services), etc.   23 
- UE Information, used for monitoring of UE information changes, triggering E2 Control, location tracking, etc.  24 
- On Demand Report, used for reporting Cell related, E2 Node related and UE related information to Near -RT RIC 25 
when requested by Near-RT RIC. 26 
NOTE: Only the UE with user consent can be configured to report location information.  27 
6.2.2 INSERT service 28 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following INSERT services: 29 
- Radio Bearer Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control DRB QoS modification, QoS flow to DRB 30 
(re)mapping, Logical channel (re)configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP 31 
duplication control, etc. 32 
- Radio Resource Allocation Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control Discontinuous Reception 33 
(DRX), Scheduling request (SR), Semi-Persistent Scheduling (SPS), Configured Grant, Channel Quality 34 
Indicator (CQI) table, Slice level PRB quota, etc. 35 
- Connected Mode Mobility Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Handover (HO), 36 
Conditional handover (CHO), Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS) HO, etc. 37 
- Radio Access Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control parameters related to RACH back -off, 38 
RRC connection reject, RRC connection release, Access barring, UE admission, etc.  39 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 15 
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Dual Connect ivity 1 
(DC) including Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, etc.  2 
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Carrier 3 
Aggregation (CA) involving secondary cell re-selection. 4 
- Idle Mode Mobility Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control intra -frequency, inter-frequency, 5 
inter-RAT cell reselection priority, idle timers, etc. 6 
6.2.3 CONTROL service 7 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following CONTROL services: 8 
- Radio Bearer Control, used for DRB QoS modification, QoS flow to DRB (re)mapping, Logical channel 9 
(re)configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP duplication control, etc.  10 
- Radio Resource Allocation Control, used to control Discontinuous Reception (DRX), Scheduling request (SR), 11 
Semi-Persistent Scheduling (SPS), Configured Grant, Channel Quality Indicator (CQI) table,  Slice level PRB 12 
quota, etc. 13 
- Connected Mode Mobility Control, used to control operations of Handover (HO), Conditional handover (CHO), 14 
Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS) HO, etc. 15 
- Radio Access Control, used for modification of RACH back-off, RRC connection reject, RRC connection 16 
release, Access barring, UE admission, etc. 17 
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Control, used to control operations of Dual Connectivity (DC) including Change of 18 
bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, etc. 19 
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Control, used to control operations of Carrier Aggregation (CA) . 20 
- Idle Mode Mobility Control, used for modification of intra-frequency, inter-frequency, inter-RAT cell 21 
reselection priority, idle timers, etc.  22 
- UE to RAN UE group assignment, used to support POLICY services. 23 
6.2.4 POLICY service 24 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following POLICY services: 25 
- Radio Bearer Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DRB QoS control, QoS flow to 26 
DRB mapping, Logical channel configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and P DCP 27 
duplication control, etc. 28 
- Radio Resource Allocation Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DRX, SR, SPS, 29 
Configured Grant, CQI table, Slice level PRB quota, etc. 30 
- Connected Mode Mobility Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to HO, CHO, DAPS 31 
HO, etc. for both serving and target RAN nodes. 32 
- Radio Access Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to RACH back- off, RRC connection 33 
reject, RRC connection release, Access barring, UE admission, etc. 34 
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DC related operations 35 
for both master and secondary RAN nodes, Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, 36 
etc. 37 
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to CA related operations 38 
for both primary and secondary cells. 39 
- Idle Mode Mobility Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to intra -frequency, inter-40 
frequency, inter-RAT cell reselection priority, inactivity timers, etc. 41 
6.3 REPORT service description 42 
The E2SM-RC REPORT service requirements defined in Section 6.2.1 are offered using a set of REPORT Styles.  All 43 
REPORT styles are implemented using a set of IEs for Action Definition, RIC Indication Header and RIC Indication 44 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 16 
Message and have specific Event Trigger approach. For each Report style, a single RAN Parameter table is used to 1 
specify the required information to be reported. 2 
The following REPORT styles are supported:  3 
- Message copy: This REPORT style is initiated by “Message Event” Event Trigger and is used to report complete 4 
NI or RRC message along with UE associated information when the event trigger conditions are satisfied.  5 
- Call Process Outcome: This REPORT style is initiated by the corresponding "Call Process Breakpoint" Event 6 
Trigger and is used to report on the outcome of a call process providing information on current, and in certain 7 
cases previous, UE or E2 Node information depending upon the nature of the target call process.   8 
- E2 Node Information: This REPORT style is initiated by “E2 Node Information Change” Event Trigger and is 9 
used to report cell related and E2 Node related information upon event trigger conditions are satisfied.  10 
- UE information: This REPORT style is initiated by “UE Information Change” Event Trigger and is used to 11 
report UE related information and UE state variables upon the event trigger conditions are satisfied.  12 
- On demand report: This REPORT style is initiated by “On Demand” Event Trigger and is used to report cell -13 
related and UE-related information on an adhoc basis upon request from Near-RT RIC. 14 
6.4 INSERT service description 15 
The E2SM-RC INSERT service requirements defined in Section 6.2.2 are offered using a set of INSERT Styles. Each 16 
style corresponds to a set of “INSERT Indications”, where each “INSERT Indication” deals with a specific functionality  17 
and has a set of associated RAN parameters, provided in a mapping table. All I NSERT Service styles are implemented 18 
using a set of IEs that constitute “Action Definition”, “RIC Indication Header” and “RIC Indication Message” to deliver 19 
RAN Control-related INSERT services. Each INSERT service style is associated with a specific “Event  Trigger” 20 
approach.  An “INSERT Indication” is used to request the RIC to control a functionality associated with the respective 21 
INSERT service style, and to set or modify the values of one or more associated RAN parameters.  22 
As an example, upon the arrival of an RRC Measurement Report in the E2 node due to the occurrence of an A3 event 23 
pertaining to a UE (which constitutes the event trigger), the E2 node can send a  message to the RIC using the 24 
“Connected Mode Mobility” INSERT service style and the “Handove r Control Request” INSERT Indication along with 25 
the “target cell ID” parameter. This RIC should then accept/deny the “Handover Control Request”, and if it accepts, it 26 
should set the value of the “target cell ID” parameter and send a CONTROL action back to the RIC. Up until then, the 27 
E2 node suspends the ongoing call processing for the UE.  28 
6.5 CONTROL service description 29 
The E2SM-RC CONTROL service requirements defined in Section 6.2.3 are offered using a set of CONTROL Styles. 30 
Each style corresponds to a set of “CONTROL Action”, where each “CONTROL Action” deals with a specific 31 
functionality and has a set of associated RAN parameters, provided in a mapping table. All CONTROL Service styles 32 
are implemented using a set of IEs constituting a “RIC Control Reque st Header” and a “RIC Control Request Message” 33 
to deliver RAN Control-related CONTROL services. A “CONTROL Action” containing one or more RAN parameters 34 
and their associated values can either be sent from the RIC, either asynchronously to the E2 node or as  a response to a 35 
previous “INSERT Indication” from the E2 node.  36 
Referring to the previous example in Section 6.4, the RIC sends a “CONTROL action” that accepts/denies the incoming 37 
“INSERT Indication” requesting for “Handover Control”, along with the value  of the “Target Primary Cell”. As another 38 
example, the RIC can also asynchronously send a “CONTROL action” asking the E2 node to configure the UE in 39 
Carrier Aggregation mode and setup one or more secondary cells to the UE, whose values are assigned by the RIC via 40 
the “CONTROL action”. 41 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 17 
6.6 POLICY service description 1 
6.6.1 Overview 2 
The E2SM-RC POLICY service requirements defined in Section 6.2.4 are offered using a set of POLICY Styles.  Each 3 
style is implemented using multiple "Policy Approach" strategies, each with a specific methodology defined to use the 4 
E2AP IE "Action Definition" to deliver RAN Control related POLICY services.  5 
The following Policy Approaches are defined: 6 
- Control: POLICY for a given Style and Action ID is defined as a single case of a s pecific Policy condition with 7 
the corresponding Policy Action defined using the same data structure as CONTROL which would be used to 8 
replace default RAN behaviour. 9 
- Offset: POLICY for a given Style and Action ID is defined as a set of different cases app licable for a range of 10 
different Policy conditions with the corresponding Policy Action defined using the dedicated data structure 11 
defined for POLICY which would be used to modify default RAN behaviour.  12 
6.6.2 Policy approach "Control" 13 
The “control” Policy Approach is similar to the CONTROL service, with static conditions and actions in the RIC 14 
Subscription used to select an appropriate CONTROL Action. When a set of Policy conditions are satisfied, then E2 15 
Node is instructed to execute a Policy Action with a set of supplementary or default set of RAN parameters. 16 
A single Policy Action shall be a result of execution of multiple policy conditions.  17 
- Each Policy Condition is defined using a combination of RAN Parameters and conditional tests associated with 18 
UE and Call process related information. 19 
- Each Policy Action is defined with a single Policy Action ID (command) which instructs E2 Node to perform a 20 
certain action when the conditions are satisfied. The Policy Action ID shall be supplemented with a set of R AN 21 
Parameters which may be used to provide information on default values to E2 Node.  22 
Examples include: 23 
- Connected mode mobility policy, Handover Execution: Message Arrival breakpoint event trigger is defined to 24 
initiate the Policy service. On the arrival of A3 Measurement Report, the Policy service kicks in. Policy service 25 
installs a set of Policy Conditions like RSRP > ‘x’ db + Target Node Load < ‘x’ value + Number of successful 26 
HO to target Node > ‘x’ value. When these Policy conditions are satisfied, then perform Policy Action -  27 
“Execute HO” defined in the CONTROL service in Section 6.5. The Policy Action may be provided as a 28 
standalone Policy Action ID “Execute HO” without any RAN parameters. As an alternative, Policy Action 29 
“Execute HO” may be supplemented with default RAN parameters like Handover only QCI 5 and 9 bearers.  30 
- Carrier Aggregation Policy, CA Release decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to initiate 31 
the POLICY service. The call process breakpoint shall define conditions for Buffer occupancy. A call process 32 
breakpoint event shall be triggered when the Buffer Occupancy (BO) < ‘x’ KB. In this scenario, the event trigger 33 
satisfies the Policy condition. Hence there is no need to define a Policy condition in the Poli cy service, When the 34 
BO < ‘x’ KB kicks in, then Policy Action shall instruct E2 Node to “Release Scell” . 35 
6.6.3 Policy Approach "Offset" 36 
The "offset" Policy Approach is based on the design assumption that the Policy Action IE is used to carry one or more 37 
RAN Parameters that are used to modify default E2 Node behaviour via the addition of an "offset" to be applied to 38 
given target threshold or other parameter used in the target call process.   39 
The applicable Policy Action is dependent upon a set of Policy Conditions and a given POLICY service may support 40 
one or more Policy conditions and so provide a targeted Policy Action for a range of diffe rent specific cases, each 41 
defined using a unique Policy condition where: 42 
- Each Policy Condition is defined using a combination of RAN Parameters and conditional tests associated with 43 
UE and Call process related information.  The first positive match in a list of Policy conditions is used to select 44 
the corresponding Policy Action. 45 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 18 
- Each Policy Action is defined using a list of RAN Parameters of data type INTEGER or REAL which may to 1 
used directly for default values of type INTEGER or REAL (i.e. Default+Off set) and indirectly to for default 2 
values of type ENUMERATED (i.e. select value in list that is Offset before or after default value).   3 
Examples include: 4 
- Connected mode mobility policy, Handover decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to 5 
initiate the POLICY service from within the call process handling UE measurement reports related to handover 6 
decisions for a specific target Slice and primary cell currently subject to Traffic Steering guidance.  The Policy 7 
conditions list of RAN Parameters supports the definition of different A3 measurement threshold criteria offset 8 
values to be applied to UEs with a specific combination of slice ID, active QoS bearers, velocity and throughput 9 
and subject to overall E2 Node load and cell level load balancing requirements.  Handover is accepted if the 10 
reported A3 measurement is greater than the default A3 measurement threshold+offset.  11 
- Carrier Aggregation Policy, CA release decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to initiate the 12 
POLICY service from within the call process related to Carrier Aggregation (CA) release decisions for a specific 13 
target Slice currently subject to QoE guidance.  The Policy conditions list of RAN Parameters supports the 14 
definition of different CA release threshold criteria offset values to be applied to UEs with a specific 15 
combination of slice ID, active QoS bearers, velocity and throughput and subject to overall E2 Node load and 16 
cell level load balancing requirements.  CA release is initiated if the UE thro ughput is less than the default UE 17 
throughput threshold+offset. 18

- RIC POLICY Service styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  28

7.3.2 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 1: Message Event 4 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to detect a specific Network Interface or RRC message event in E2 5 
Node. The dection can be based on only for incoming or outgoing message. The E2 Node can also be configured to 6 
detect multiple messages simultaneously and to trigger only when all the configured message events happen or for any 7 
logical combination of message events.  8 
Each message event configured can be further conditioned to be associated only for a certain UE or group of UEs as 9 
indicated by the Associated UE Info IE if included, or only for some specific UE events defined in Section 8.1.5 as 10 
indicated by the Associated UE Event IE if included. In case that the Global Associated UE Info IE is included, the 11 
information is applied uniformly to all the message events configured and the IE shall override any Associated UE Info  12 
IE included for some message events. 13 
For each message event configured, Event Trigger Condition ID is assigned so tha t E2 Node can reply to Near-RT RIC 14 
in the RIC INDICATION message to inform which event(s) are the cause for triggering.  15 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 1 (9.2.1.1.1). 16

Each E2 Node information change configured can also be conditioned to be associated with a specific cell or group of 8 
cells for event triggering, as indicated by the Associated Cell Info IE if included.  9 
For each information change configured for event triggering, Event Trigger Condition ID is also assigned so that E2 10 
Node can reply to Near-RT RIC in the RIC INDICATION message to inform which event(s) are the cause for 11 
triggering. 12 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 3 (9.2.1.1.3). 13 
7.3.5 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 4: UE Information Change 14 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to detect UE Context related information change from the subscribed 15 
E2 Node. The E2 Node can also be configured to detect multiple changes simultaneously and to trigger only when all 16 
the configured changes happen or for any logical combination of the configured changes. 17 
In this version of E2SM-RC specification, the supported UE Context information changes for event triggering are  18 
- RRC state change 19 
- UE identifier change (based on UE ID defined in Section 9.3.10)  20 
- RLC/PDCP state variable or MAC state variable change (based on RAN Parameters defined in Sections 8.1.1.4 21 
and 8.1.1.8) 22 
For UE identifier change, the following cases are supported for event triggering.  23 
UE Identifier 
Change ID 
UE Identifier Change 
Type 
Description 
1 New UE Connected Triggered when new UE ID is assigned for a new UE connected.  
2 UE Handed Over Triggered when new UE ID is assigned due to HO from another node. 
3 UE ID Changed Triggered when any content of the assigned UE ID (based on the 
definition of UE ID in Section 9.3.10) has changed.  
4 UE ID Removed Triggered when a UE is released, and its UE ID is removed. 
Table 7.3.5-1: Event Trigger Definition Style 4 – Supported UE Identifier changes 24 
The detection for each UE information change configured can be based on for any UEs, or only for a certain UE or 25 
group of UEs as indicated by the Associated UE Info IE if included. 26 
For each information change configured, Event Trigger Condition ID is assigned so that E2 Node can reply to Near-RT 27 
RIC in the RIC INDICATION message to inform which event(s) are the cause for triggering.  28 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 4 (9.2.1.1.4). 29

 22 
7.3.6 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 5: On Demand 1 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to be immediately triggered by E2 Node when a RIC subscription 2 
having this event trigger is accepted. Once accepted, the E2 Node shall consider that this RIC subscription shall expire 3 
automatically once all the requested actions for this RIC subscription are performed by the E2 Node.  4 
The event can be further conditioned to be associated only for a certain UE or group of UEs as indicated by the 5 
Associated UE Info IE if included, or for a specific cell or group of cells as indicated by the Associated Cell Info IE if 6 
included. In this case, Near-RT RIC shall ensure that additional conditions imposed by the Associated UE Info IE or 7 
Associated Cell Info IE does not prevent event triggering as soon as the RIC subscription is accepted by the E2 Node. 8 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses the RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 5 (9.2.1.1.5). 9

7.4 Supported RIC REPORT Services 11 
7.4.1 REPORT Service style list 12 
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description 
1 Message copy This style is used to report a copy of complete Network Interface or 
RRC message. 
2 Call Process Outcome This style is used to report the outcome of an ongoing call process. 
3 E2 Node Information This style is used to report E2 Node information, Serving Cell 
Configuration and Neighbour Relation related information. 
4 UE Information This style is used to report the UE related information like PDCP, 
RLC, MAC UE state variables and RRC UE State. 
5 On Demand Report This style is used to report snapshot of UE related information and 
Cell related information upon request from Near-RT RIC. 
 13 
7.4.2 REPORT Service Style 1: Message Copy 14 
7.4.2.1 REPORT Service Style description 15 
This REPORT Service style provides the complete copy of a Network Interface or RRC message to be carried as a 16 
transparent container in the RIC Indication Message IE. 17 
This REPORT service style may also be used to report UE specific information associated with the Network 18 
Interface/RRC messages as provided in Section 8.2.1 RAN Parameters. Examples include reporting of UEID to Near -19 
RT RIC when UE attaches to the E2 Node or when the UEID changes during Xn Handover, UE events like Secon dary 20 
Cell addition, Arrival of A3 Measurement Report (see Section 8.1.5 for the list of UE events).  21 
This REPORT Service style is initiated by Event Trigger style 1: Message Event . 22 
7.4.2.2 REPORT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 23 
The Action Definition for this service style is used to request E2 Node to report a copy of NI and/or RRC message and 24 
may be used to report UE specific information. The action definition indicates which related UE information is to be 25 
reported along with the NI or RRC message that triggers this report service. 26 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 1 (9.2.1.2.1). The supported Parameters for this 27 
format are provided in Section 8.2.1. 28 
7.4.2.3 REPORT Service RIC Indication Header IE contents 29 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Indication Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.3.1) 30

7.4.4 REPORT Service Style 3: E2 Node Information.   26 
7.4.4.1 REPORT Service Style description 27

provided by E2AP [3]. The information is carried in the RIC Indication Message IE along with an associated RIC 29 
Indication Header IE providing information related event trigger conditions. The required information to be provided is 30 
controlled using the associated RIC Action Definition IE parameters. 31 
This REPORT Service style provides information related to: 32 
- Serving Cell configuration 33 
- Neighbour Relation Information  34 
whenever the corresponding event trigger for change in information content is satisfied. With every change in the 35 
information content of the Neighbour Relation Information, complete list of Neighbour relation table is sent to Near -RT 36 
RIC with indicaton on the modified information. 37 
This REPORT Service style is initiated by Event Trigger style 3: E2 Node Information Change . 38

information. The E2AP RIC Subscription Delete procedure or RIC Subscription Delete Required procedure [3] is not 15 
required to delete this subscription. The reporting shall be per UE based or per cell based depending on the information 16 
requested to be reported. 17

7.5.2 INSERT Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control Request 7 
7.5.2.1 INSERT Service Style description 8 
This INSERT Service style provides a mechanism to initiate request to the RIC for controlling the functionalities of a 9 
radio bearer related process pertaining to a UE using the RIC Indication Message IE and associated RIC Indication 10 
Header IE. The E2 node sends a RIC Indication message to the near-RT RIC and the ongoing call process is suspended 11 
at the E2 node until the E2 node hears back from the RIC. The optional RIC Call Process ID  IE is used by the E2 node 12 
to match a RIC Control Request message to a RIC Indication message, following which the E2 node can resume the 13 
suspended call processing for the UE.   14 
Applications of this service include: 15 
- Request for DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization 16 
targets. 17 
- Request for QoS Flow (re)mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  18 
- Request for Logical channel (re)configuration 19 
- Request for Radio Bearer Admission Control, to configure DRB admission control such as reject or release may 20 
be applied. 21 
- Request for Split bearer and PDCP duplication control 22 
This Insert style supports the following Indication services, each service listed below with a corresponding Indication 23 
ID. The RAN parameters, associated with each Insert Indication service, are listed in t he sections shown below. 24

7.5.2.2 INSERT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 2 
This INSERT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 3 (9.2.1.2.3). This Insert style deals with the 3 
supported Indication services, each service with a corresponding Indication ID listed in Section 7.5.2.1. The RAN 4 
parameters, associated with each Insert RIC Indication service,  are included by the E2 node in the RIC Indication 5 
message. Via the RIC Indication message, the E2 node seeks the near-RT RIC to accept or deny the request raised by 6 
the E2 node and to accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters by the RIC via the control action in 7 
the ensuing RIC Control Request message from the RIC. 8

request raised by the E2 node and accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters, via the control action 16

7.5.6 INSERT Service Style 5: Dual Connectivity Control Request 5 
7.5.6.1 INSERT Service Style description 6 
This INSERT Service style provides a mechanism to initiate request for controlling the dual connectivity of the UE 7 
using the RIC Indication Message IE and associated RIC Indication Header IE. The E2 node sends a RIC Indication 8 
message to the near-RT RIC and the ongoing call process is suspended at the E2 node until the E2 node hears back from 9 
the RIC. The optional RIC Call Process ID IE is used by the E2 node to match a RIC Control Request message to a RIC 10 
Indication message, following which the E2 node can resume the suspended call processing for the UE. 11 
Applications of this service include: 12 
- Request for Dual connectivity (EN-DC, MR-DC or NR-NR DC) initiation for a selected UE towards a target 13 
secondary cell (PScell) 14 
- Request for Secondary cell change for a selected UE towards a target secondary cell (PScell)  15 
- Request for Dual connectivity (EN-DC, MR-DC or NR-NR DC) modification for a selected UE  16 
- Request for Dual connectivity (EN-DC, MR-DC or NR-NR DC) release initiation for a selected UE 17 
- Request for Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types for a selected UE  18 
This Insert style supports the following Indication services, each service listed below with a corresponding Indication 19 
ID. The RAN parameters, associated with each Insert Indication service, are listed in the sections shown below.  20 
Indication 
ID 
Indication 
Name 
Insert Indication Description Associated 
RAN 
parameters 
1 DC Secondary 
Node  
Addition Control 
request 
To request secondary node addition for dual connectivity 8.3.6.1 
2 DC Secondary 
Node 
Modification and 
Release Control 
request 
To request modification of secondary node for DC 8.3.6.2 
3 DC PSCell

another secondary node 
8.3.6.3

7.5.6.2 INSERT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 22 
This INSERT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 3 (9.2.1.2.3). The Insert style deals with the 23 
supported Indication services, each service with a corresponding Indication ID listed in Section 7.5.6.1. The RAN 24 
parameters, associated with each Insert Indication service, are included by the E2 node in the RIC Indication message. 25 
Via the RIC Indication message, the E2 node seeks the near-RT RIC to accept or deny the request raised by the E2 node 26 
and to accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters by the RIC via the control action in the ensuing 27 
RIC Control Request message from the RIC.  28

7.6 Supported RIC CONTROL Services 8 
7.6.1 CONTROL Service Style Types 9 
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description 
1 Radio Bearer control Used to modify the configuration the Radio Bearer Control (RBC) 
related parameters and/or behaviours at the E2 Node for a 
specific UE 
2 Radio resource allocation 
control 
Used to modify the configuration the Radio Resource Allocation 
control related parameters and/or behaviours at the E2 Node for a 
specific E2 Node, cell, slice, UE and/or QoS 
3 Connected mode mobility 
control  
Used to initiate a connected mode mobility procedure (Handover 
or Conditional Handover), optionally with Dual Active Protocol 
Stack (DAPS), for a specific UE towards either a target cell (for 
HO) or a list of candidate cells (for CHO) 
4 Radio access control Used to modify Radio access related functions used to control UE 
access to cells 
5 Dual connectivity (DC) control Used to initiate Dual connectivity (DC) mechanisms 
6 Carrier Aggregation (CA) 
control 
Used to initiate Carrier Aggregation (CA) mechanisms 
7 Idle mode mobility control Used to modify Idle mode mobility related functions used to control 
UE reselection of cells 
8 UE information and 
assignment 
Used for Explicit UE list assignment, UE information report 
generation and to complete UE identification.  These services are 
used to support other RIC services. 
 10 
Each of the Control Service Styles 1-8 listed above points to adopt the following common features: 11 
- Control Action ID: The index ID for the individual control action under a given Control Service style.  12 
- Control Action Name: Indicates the functionality of the E2 node which is controlled by Near -RT RIC 13 
- Control Action Description: Describes the control action and functionality of the receiving E2 Node. 14 
- Associated RAN parameters: Identifies the RAN parameters to be controlled by Near -RT RIC pertaining to the 15 
given control action. 16 
The details of the individual Control Service Styles are provided in subsequent se ctions. 17 
7.6.2 CONTROL Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control 18 
7.6.2.1 CONTROL Service Style description 19 
This CONTROL Service style provides a mechanism to initiate or resume a radio bearer control related process using 20 
the RIC Control Message IE and associated RIC Control Header IE and the optional RIC Call Process ID IE used when 21 
resuming a call process following a previous INSERT service. The corresponding INSERT service is service style 1 22 
covered in Section 7.5.2.   23 
Applications of this service include: 24

- DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization targets.  1 
- QoS Flow (re)mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  2 
- Logical channel (re)configuration 3 
- Radio Bearer Admission Control, to configure DRB admission control such as reject or release may be applied  4 
- Split bearer and PDCP duplication control 5

7.6.2.2 CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contents 8 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE has the UE ID IE, the Control Service Style ID, the Control Action 9 
ID IE and the RIC Control Decision IE that indicates whether the RIC accepts or rejects the INDICATION request from 10 
the previous incoming INSERT indication, if any (with matching RAN Call Process ID IE), from the E2 node.  11 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.6.1). 12 
7.6.2.3 CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contents 13 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contains the sequence of RAN parameters, associated with a given 14 
Control Action within this Control Service style, controlled by the near-RT RIC along with the values for these 15 
parameters, as set by the RIC. 16 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Message IE Format 1 (9.2.1.7.1). 17 
 18 
If there is a previous INSERT Indication Request to the RIC, then the corresponding Control Action ID used by the RIC 19 
for the ensuing CONTROL Request message is the one that matches the Insert Indication ID, among the ones provided 20 
in the table shown in Section 7.6.2.1.  It is to be noted that the control action “Radio admission control” (corresponding 21 
to control action ID 4) is used only as a response to an incoming INSERT indication with the corresponding service 22 
style and indication request ID and cannot be used asynchronously without a previous INSERT indication. 23 
7.6.2.4 CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE contents 24 
This CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE contains identifier used by the Near-RT RIC to allow the RAN 25 
Function to match the outgoing INSERT Service message with a subsequent incoming CONTROL Service message. 26

processing the incoming RIC Control Request message. However, this does not reflect the outcome of the call 4 
processing upon receiving the message.   5

7.6.6 CONTROL Service Style 5: Dual Connectivity Control 2 
7.6.6.1 CONTROL Service Style description 3 
This CONTROL Service style provides a mechanism to initiate or resume a dual connectivity control related process 4 
using the RIC Control Message IE and associated RIC Control Header IE and the optional RIC Call Process ID IE used 5 
when resuming a call process following a previous INSERT service.  The corresponding INSERT service is service 6 
style 5 covered in Section 7.5.6. 7 
Applications of this service include: 8 
- Dual connectivity (EN-DC, MR-DC or NR-NR DC) initiation for a selected UE towards a target secondary cell 9 
(PScell) 10 
- Secondary cell change for a selected UE towards a target secondary cell (PScell)  11 
- Dual connectivity (EN-DC, MR-DC or NR-NR DC) modification for a selected UE  12 
- Dual connectivity (EN-DC, MR-DC or NR-NR DC) release initiation for a selected UE 13 
- Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types for a selected UE  14 
The supported RAN control actions and the corresponding RAN parameters are as follows. 15 
Control 
Action 
ID 
Control Action 
Name 
Control Action Description Associated 
RAN 
parameters 
1 DC Secondary 
Node  
Addition Control 
To control secondary node addition for dual connectivity 8.4.6.1 
2 DC Secondary 
Node 
Modification 
and release 
Control 
To control modification and release of secondary node for DC 8.4.6.2 
3 DC PSCell 
Change control 
To control PSCell change of a UE within a secondary node or to another 
secondary node 
8.4.6.3 
4 DC Secondary 
Node Change 
Control 
To control changing the secondary node of a UE for DC 8.4.6.4 
 16 
7.6.6.2 CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contents 17 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE has the UE ID IE, the Control Service Style ID, the Control Action 18 
ID IE and the RIC Control Decision IE that indicates whether the RIC accepts or rejects the INDICATION request from 19 
the previous incoming INSERT indication, if any (with matching RAN Call Process ID IE), from the E2 node.  20 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.6.1). 21

7.6.6.3 CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contents 1 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contains the sequence of RAN parameters, associated with a given 2 
Control Action within this Control Service style, controlled by the near-RT RIC along with the values for these 3 
parameters, as set by the RIC.  4 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Message IE Format 1 (9.2.1.7.1). 5 
 6 
If there is a previous INSERT Indication Request to the RIC, then the corresponding Control Action ID used by the RIC 7 
for the ensuing CONTROL Request message is the one that matches the Insert Indication ID, among the ones provided 8 
in the table shown in Section 7.6.6.1. 9 
7.6.6.4 CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE contents 10 
This CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE contains identifier used by the Near-RT RIC to allow the RAN 11 
Function to match the outgoing INSERT Service message with a subsequent incoming CONTROL Service message. 12 
This CONTROL Service style uses RIC Call Process ID IE Format 1 (9.2.1.5.1). 13 
7.6.6.5 CONTROL Service RIC Control Outcome IE contents 14 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Outcome IE contains a transparent container that is used to carry the outcome of 15 
processing the incoming RIC Control Request message. However, this does not reflect the outcome of the call 16 
processing upon receiving the message.   17 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Outcome IE Format 1 (9.2.1.8.1). 18

7.6.9 CONTROL Service Style 8: UE information and assignment 2 
7.6.9.1 CONTROL Service Style description 3 
This CONTROL Service style provides a mechanism to both directly and indirectly monitor and control UE 4 
information and to add or remove explicit UE assignments to Explicit UE lists.   5 
Applications of this service include: 6 
- UE to Explicit UE list assignment command: Used to Add or Remove the nominated UE to the Explicit UE list 7 
name, also used to request list of supported Explicit UE list 8 
- UE information request: Used to obtain UE information including list of Explicit UE List assignments 9 
- UE identification request: Used to complete UE identification 10 
The supported RAN control actions and the corresponding RAN parameters are as follows. 11 
Control 
Action 
ID 
Control Action 
Name 
Required information RAN Parameter

list of supported Explicit UE list) 
8.4.9.1 
 12 
7.6.9.2 CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contents 13 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contains the UE ID IE, RIC Style Type IE and Control Action ID IE. 14 
There is no previous INSERT Indication request from the E2 node for this service style.  15 
Note that for RIC Action ID =3 "UE identification request", the UE ID IE in the RIC Control Header IE shall contain 16 
information elements set to zero (for INTEGER values), all bits = 0 (for OCTET STRING) or NULL (for PRINTABLE 17 
STRING values) if information is not known. 18 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.6.1). 19 
7.6.9.3 CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contents 20 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contains a list of RAN Parameters used to support the information 21 
list of Control actions shown in Section 7.6.9.1. 22 
 23 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Message IE Format 1 (9.2.1.7.1). 24 
7.6.9.4 CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE contents 25 
This CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE is not supported for this CONTROL service style. 26

7.7 Supported RIC POLICY Services 6 
7.7.1 POLICY Service style list 7 
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description 
1 Policy for Radio Bearer 
control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of Radio 
Bearer Control (RBC) of call processes for a specific RAN UE 
Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
2 Policy for Radio resource 
allocation control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of Radio 
Resource Allocation control of call processes for a specific RAN 
UE Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
3 Policy for Connected mode 
mobility control  
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of connected 
mode mobility procedure (Handover or Conditional Handover), 
optionally with Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS), call processes 
for a specific RAN UE Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or 
QoS 
4 Policy for Radio access 
control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of radio access 
control processes 
5 Policy for Dual connectivity 
(DC) control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of dual 
connectivity (DC) call processes for a specific RAN UE Group 
based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
6 Policy for Carrier Aggregation 
(CA) control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of carrier 
aggregation (CA) call processes for a specific RAN UE Group 
based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
7 Policy for Idle mode mobility 
control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of idle mode 
configuration call processes for a specific RAN UE Group based 
on cell, slice and/or UE list. 
 8 
Each of the POLICY Service Styles 1-7 listed above are supported using the following common features: 9 
• Event Trigger: POLICY service is initiated by either Event Trigger style 1: Message Event  or Event Trigger 10 
style 2: Call process breakpoint. 11 
• A ction ID : The index ID for the individual action under a given POLICY Service style. 12 
• A ction Name: Indicates the functionality of the E2 node which is controlled by Near -RT RIC 13 
• A ction Description : Describes the action and functionality of the receiving E2 Node. 14 
• A ssociated RAN parameters: Identifies the RAN parameters to be controlled by Near -RT RIC pertaining to the 15 
given Policy action, used to define Policy Condition and RAN Imperative Policy.  16 
All POLICY Service styles use RIC Action Definition IE Format 2 (9.2.1.2.2) which provides the policy conditions and 17 
corresponding Policy Action. All of these factors are defined as a sequence of RAN Parameters assigned according to a 18 
given Policy Style and Policy Action where: 19 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 47 
- Policy Action ID is a Policy specific identifier of a specific Action for a specific Policy style. 1 
- Policy Condition is a Policy specific condition to select a specific Policy Action. Policy Condition is described in 2 
terms of a list of test conditions concerning UE and E2 Node information selection criteria using RAN 3 
Parameters defined with a Conditional Criteria Definition. Default RAN behaviour is to be applied to any UE 4 
when none of the Policy conditions are met. 5 
- Policy Action is encoded in terms of a list of specific RAN Parameters and shall be applied to any UE within a 6 
given RAN UE Group that meets a specific Policy Condition.   7 
The details of the individual POLICY Service Styles and specific Policy Actions are provided in subsequent sections.  8 
7.7.2 POLICY Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control 9 
7.7.2.1 POLICY Service Style description 10 
This POLICY Service style provides an Imperative Policy to control execution of a radio bearer control related 11 
process.   12 
Applications of this service include: 13 
- DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization targets.  14 
- QoS Flow mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  15 
- Logical channel configuration 16 
- Radio Bearer Admission, to guide DRB admission control algorithms for admission and/or rejection of DRB 17 
requests 18 
- DRB termination 19 
- DRB Split bearer 20 
- PDCP duplication control 21 
7.7.2.2 POLICY Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 22

8 RAN Parameter assignments 1 
8.0 Approach 2 
The RAN parameters associated with each RIC service  described in Section 7 are listed  here in Section 8 .  Each RAN 3 
parameter belongs to one of the following value types: 4 
• ELEMENT: a singleton variable, which does not have any other associated RAN parameters.  5 
• STRUCTURE: a sequence of RAN parameters, each of which can be either an ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE 6 
or a LIST 7 
• LIST: a list of STRUCTURES, where each STRUCTURE is as defined above. The sequence of RAN parameters 8 
is the same across all the STRUCTURES within the list. 9 
The corresponding 3GPP standard definitions of these RAN parameters (if available) are referenced in the tables below 10 
under the “RAN Parameter Definition” column. These RAN parameters having 3GPP standard definitions are not freshly 11 
defined or redefined here.  12 
Note that only those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT are subject to test conditions by the RIC in the “Event 13 
Trigger Definition”.  14 
Any RAN parameter within a STRUCTURE or LIST shall not be reference d individually. Hierarchy of a LIST or a 15 
STRUCTURE shall be traversed to access any RAN parameter within the LIST or STRUCTURE  16 
Note that a RAN parameter may be associated with as a key where its corresponding Key Flag  is set to “TRUE”. These 17 
RAN parameters serve as a reference to other RAN parameters within a structure that may be a part of LIST to enable 18 
the E2 Node interpret the scope of RAN parameters that are controlled by Near -RT RIC. 19 
If the “key flag” is specified in the RIC Event Trigger Definition, then the RAN parameters corresponding to “that specific 20 
itemized structure” in the list indexed by the “key flag” are subject to test condition, but if the “key flag” is not mentioned 21 
in the RIC Event Trigger Definition, then the RAN parameters correspondi ng to “any itemized structure” within the list 22 
are subject to test condition.  23 
For e.g., The ‘QFI’ can be considered a ‘key parameter’ to identify a QoS flow among the list of flows in a UE -specific 24 
PDU session. If the QFI parameter is NOT mentioned and the RIC subscribes to an event pertaining to 5QI 8, then “any 25 
QoS flow” in the list of flows of a PDU session for the UE that matches the condition of 5QI being equal to 8 would be 26 
covered by this event trigger definition. On the other hand, if the QFI parameter is mentioned in the event trigger 27 
definition, then only that specific QoS flow pertaining to the indicated QFI within the list is covered  28 
8.1 RAN parameters for Event Trigger 29 
The RAN Parameters pertaining to “Event Trigger” that are used across multiple service styles are listed here. All RAN 30 
Parameters defined in section 8.1 may also be used to define Policy Condition, see also section 8.5.  31 
8.1.1 Common RAN Parameters 32 
This section contains the common set of RAN parameters that can be accessed via RAN parameters defined in each 33 
service style across multiple services. 34

8.3.9.2 E2 Node Context Information 1 
The associated RAN parameters are given in Section 8.1.1.11. 2 
8.3.10 Indication Semantics Description for interpretation by the RIC 3 
The E2 node requests the near-RT RIC for the following services as far as the radio bearer Control request is concerned.  4 
(a) In the RIC Indication Header IE, the E2 node indicates the Insert Indication ID, that is associated with the Insert 5 
Service Style ID for the radio bearer control request, along with the UE ID, so as to enable the RIC to interpret 6 
which Insert Indication service pertaining to which UE is being requested by the E2 node.  7 
(b) In the RIC Indication Message IE, the E2 node indicates the list of the RAN parameters in the Indication 8 
message that it wants to be controlled by the near-RT RIC. If the E2 node does not provide values for these 9 
parameters in the RIC Indication message IE, then the RIC would set the values for these parameters in the 10 
control action sent via the RIC Control Request message, along with its decision to accept/deny the request 11 
raised by the E2 node (indicated in the RIC Indication Header IE). If the RAN parameter indicated by the E2 12 
node is an ELEMENT, the RIC would set the value for the parameter in its RIC Control Request message. If the 13 
indicated RAN parameter is a STRUCTURE but if the E2 node does not list any constitutent RAN parameter of 14 
the STRUCTURE, then the RIC would set the values for all the constitutent RAN parameters of the 15 
STRUCTURE. If the parameter is a LIST, then: 16 
a. If the E2 node also indicates the Key RAN parameter pertaining to the itemized STRUCTURE in the 17 
LIST, then the RIC would set the values for all constituent RAN parameters within the structure, pointed 18 
by the key. 19 
b. If the E2 node does not indicate the Key RAN parameter pertaining to the itemized STRUCTURE in the 20 
LIST, then the RIC would set the values for all constituent RAN parameters within eac h itemized 21 
STRUCTURE, whose key RAN parameter is identified by the RIC. 22 
(c) If the E2 node provides values for these parameters in the RIC Indication message IE, then the RIC would set the 23 
values only for those indicated parameters for which it would choos e to replace the values already set by the E2 24 
node. It also communicates its decision to accept/deny the request raised by the E2 node for the DRB.  25 
(d) Any RAN parameter identified as a key shall always carry a value set by the E2 node, if the E2 node expects the 26 
RIC to control the parameters pertaining to the STRUCTURE pointed by the E2 node. The value of this key 27 
RAN parameter is an index that points to the entire STRUCTURE, and hence the value of the key RAN 28 
parameter cannot be modified by the near-RT RIC. Without indicating the value for the key RAN parameter, the 29 
RIC would not control the parameters associated with the structure indexed by the key . 30 
Note that the RIC can only set the values for those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT when they are in dicated 31 
by the E2 node; however, these RAN parameters can be contained with a STRUCTURE or within an itemized 32 
STRUCTURE in a LIST. Also, if the DRB ID key parameter is not present for any DRB in the RIC Indication Message 33 
IE, then the RIC would discard the RIC Indication message. And the E2 node would have to set values based on its 34 
default radio resource management policies upon time out, and continue with the ongoing call processing. Hence, 35 
indicating the DRB ID IE for the DRB(s) is a pre-requisite for the RIC to act on the Insert indication via its RIC Control 36 
Request message. 37

8.4.2.6 DRB Split Ratio Control 1 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the presence of Downlink PDCP Data Split IE, the E2 node shall 2 
split the downlink PDCP traffic between the Master Node and Secondary Node over the X2/Xn interface based on the 3 
recommended ratio. In the presence of Uplink PDCP Data Split Threshold IE, the E2 node shall invoke procedures 4 
related to DRB Split Ratio Control, such as Bearer Context Management, UE Context Management, RRC Message 5 
Transfer, etc. and include the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the relate d interface 6 
messages. If the DRB ID is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure .  7

8.4.3.5 CQI table configuration 2 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node shall invoke procedures related to Scheduling Request 3 
Parameter Configuration, such as RRC Message Transfer, etc. and include the IEs corresponding to one or more of 4 
parameters described below in the related interface messages. If the CSI Report Config ID is missing in the RIC Control 5 
Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure. 6

8.4.3.6 Slice-level PRB quota 2 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node allocates slice-specific PRB quota for the indicated S-3 
NSSAI in terms of the maximum PRB allocation ratio, minimum PRB allocation ratio and dedicated PRB allocation 4 
ratio for the given slice among the available set of PRBs. If the S-NSSAI is missing in the RIC Control Request message, 5 
the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure. 6

8.4.4 Connected Mode Mobility Control 3 
8.4.4.1 Handover Control 4 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of Xn/X2 or NG or inter-RAT handovers, the E2 node 5 
shall invoke procedures, such as Handover Preparation related to UE Mobility Management, Bearer Context 6 
Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. In the case of intra-gNB or F1 handover, the E2 7 
node shall invoke procedures, such as UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 node includes the 8 
IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages. If the Target 9 
Primary Cell ID IE is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure 10 
message. 11

8.4.4.2 Conditional Handover Control 2 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of Xn/X2 or NG or inter-RAT conditional handovers, the 3 
E2 node shall invoke procedures, such as Handover Preparation related to UE Mobility Management, Bearer Context 4 
Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. involving the candidate target cells (note that there 5 
is only one Handover Preparation in the case of NG or inter-RAT handovers). In the case of intra-gNB or F1 6 
conditional handover, the E2 node shall invoke procedures, such as UE Context Modification , RRC Message Transfer, 7 
etc. The E2 node includes the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface 8 
messages. If the Target Cell IE is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control 9 
Failure message. 10

8.5 RAN parameters for POLICY services 6 
8.5.1 Approach 7 
The RAN parameters associated with each policy action being controlled by Near -RT RIC described in Section 7.7 are 8 
listed.   9 
There are two types of E2 policies: 10 
i) Control action policy: In this type, the near-RT RIC tells the E2 node on the specific per-UE control action that 11 
needs to be performed, upon meeting a given policy condition for a given UE or a group of UEs, for a given cell 12 
and/or for a given E2 node. This policy type is descriptive in nature. The control action is defined with respect to 13 
individual UEs and UE-specific bearers, flows, PDU sessions, etc.  14 
ii) Offset based policy: In this type, the near-RT RIC offers a generic prescriptive guidance to the E2 node on how 15 
it shall deviate from default behaviour via the application of offset parameters provided in the POLICY Action 16 
IE. Different POLICY Action IEs are associated with different POLICY conditions described in terms of UE and 17 
E2 Node characteristics. As defined in section 6.6.3, offset parameters are to be applied to default parameters 18 
according to the following rules: 19 
- INTEGER and REAL default parameters: Offset parameter have the same data type as default parameter and 20 
is added to default parameter with positive offset parameter values increasing default value and negative 21 
offset parameter values decreasing default value.  That is, policy modifies the target call process such that:  22 
Value to be applied = (Default Parameter) + (Offset Parameter)- ENUMERATED parameters: Offset 23 
parameter are of data type INTEGER and are used to select a different item in the ENUMERATED list, 24 
positive offset parameter values used to select items that are further on in the list, zero offset parameter 25 
values used to select the default value, negative offset parameter values used to select items that are earlier on 26 
in the list.  When and if the offset parameter value results in the selection of an item in the ENUMERATED 27 
list that exceeds the ENUMERATED list length then the last item in the list is selected.  When and if the 28 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 216 
offset parameter value results in the selection of an item in the ENUMERATED list that prior to the first item 1 
in the ENUMERATED list then the first item in the list is selected.  That is, policy modifies the target call 2 
process such that: 3 
ENUMERATED List index = MIN [List length-1, MAX [0, (Default Parameter) + (Offset Parameter)] ] 4 
The common set of RAN Parameters that can be used across all POLICY service styles is given in the table below.  5

9.3 Information Element definitions 2 
9.3.1 General 3 
When specifying information elements which are to be represented by bit strings, if not otherwise specifically stated in 4 
the semantics description of the concerned IE or elsewhere, the following principle applies with regards to the ordering 5 
of bits: 6 
- The first bit (leftmost bit) contains the most significant bit (MSB); 7 
- The last bit (rightmost bit) contains the least significant bit (LSB); 8 
- When importing bit strings from other specifications, the first bit of the bit string contains the first bit of the 9 
concerned information. 10 
9.3.2 RAN Function Name 11 
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.1. 12 
9.3.3 RIC Style Type 13 
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.2. 14 
9.3.4 RIC Style Name 15 
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.3. 16 
9.3.5 RIC Format Type 17 
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.4. 18

description

9.3.11 RAN Parameter Value Type 1

containing constituent elements or a list of structures. The parameters and their types are given in Section 8.4.  3 
IE/Group Name Presence Range IE type and 
reference 
Semantics description 
CHOICE RAN Parameter 
Value Type 
M  
 
A RAN Parameter can either be an 
ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE or a LIST. 
 >ELEMENT with Key Flag 
TRUE 
   If the RAN parameter is singular variable 
and if it is a key parameter with key flag 
set to TRUE as in Section 8. 
>>RAN Parameter Value M  9.3.14 This IE must be filled for both INSERT 
and CONTROL if the key flag is TRUE 
so as to reference the proper structure 
within the list. 
>ELEMENT with Key Flag 
FALSE 
   If the RAN parameter is singular variable 
and if it is NOT a key parameter (key flag 
set to FALSE). as in Section 8. 
>>RAN Parameter Value C-ifControl  9.3.14 This IE must be filled if this structure is 
part of a RIC Control Request message; 
else, if it is part of a RIC Indication 
message, this IE is optional. 
 >STRUCTURE    If the RAN parameter is a structure, in 
turn containing a set of RAN parameters. 
>>RAN Parameter Structure M  9.3.12

individual items, each of which has an 
index.

9.3.25 Logical OR  7 
This IE indicates a logical ("and” or “or”) connection of the current condition to the next condition in a given sequence 8 
of conditions.  9 
IE/Group Name Presence Range IE type and reference Semantics 
description 
Logical OR M  ENUMERATED (true, false, 
…) 
If set to “true”, 
logical connection 
to the next 
condition is “or”. 
Otherwise, “and”.

9.4 Information Element Abstract Syntax (with ASN.1) 1 
9.4.1 General 2 
E2SM-RC ASN.1 definition conforms to ITU-T Rec. X.680 [5] and ITU-T Rec. X.681 [6]. 3 
Sub clause 9.4.2 presents the Abstract Syntax of the E2SM information elements to be carried  within the E2AP [3] 4 
protocol messages with ASN.1. In case there is contradiction between the ASN.1 definition in this sub clause and the 5 
tabular format in sub clause 9.2 and 9.3, the ASN.1 shall take precedence, except for the definition of conditions for the 6 
presence of conditional elements, in which the tabular format shall take precedence. 7 
If an E2SM information element carried as an OCTET STRING in an E2AP [3] message that is not constructed as 8 
defined above is received, this shall be considered as Abstract Syntax Error, and the message shall be handled as 9 
defined for Abstract Syntax Error in clause 9. 10

Annex A: Examples on IE Contents 1 
A.1 Introduction 2 
This annex presents example applications of selected use cases showing alternative solutions using different 3 
combinations of RIC Services Report, Insert, Control and/or Policy. 4 
A.2 Connected mode mobility based on UE measurement report 5 
A.2.1 Assumptions 6 
This example is based on the following assumptions: 7 
1 O- CU-CP, or gNB for aggregated deployments, has E2 interface to Near -RT RIC and supports one or more RIC 8 
services using E2SM-RC. 9 
2 UE is in RRC CONNECTED state using NR access and has successfully attached to a 5G Core Network (5GC)  10 
3 UE has been previously configured to send RRC Measurement Reports. 11 
4 UE sends a RRC Measurement Report containing one or more neighbour cell measurements applicable for an 12 
inter-cell connected mode mobility event (i.e. a Handover) 13 
5 O- CU-CP, or gNB for aggregated deployments, uses one or more RIC Services to complete the handover 14 
decision and either execute handover (i.e. using procedure described in 3GPP 38.300 section 9.2.3) or ignores 15 
measurement report. 16 
Step 5 may be realized using one or more of the following solutions: 17 
i) According to a previously established RIC Subscription procedure, the arrival of the RRC Measurement Report 18 
triggers an Event Trigger which results in the E2 Node suspending the ongoing call process and sending a RIC 19 
Service INSERT message to the Near-RT RIC.  The Near-RT RIC takes the Handover Decision and sends a RIC 20 
Service CONTROL message carrying the response which is used by the E2 node to resume the call process.   21 
ii) According to a previously established RIC Subscription procedure the arrival of the RRC Measurement Report 22 
triggers an Event Trigger which results in the E2 Node executing a RIC Service POLICY which is used to 23 
modify the default Handover Decision and so modifies the remaining steps in the ongoing call process.  24 
 25 
A.2.2 Solution using RIC Services Insert and Control  26 
Editor’s Note: FFS 27 
A.2.3 Solution using RIC Service Policy ("Offset" based approach) 28 
This section provides a solution for the Connected Mode Mobility event call flow using the RIC Service Policy using 29 
the “Offset” approach.  Corresponding example message content are provided for the RIC Event Trigger Definition  IE 30 
and RIC Action Definition IE contents for the Connected Mode Mobility service (Policy Style 3) sent from the RIC to 31 
the E2 node to establish a policy used to provide guidance for the handling of incoming RRC Measurement reports from 32 
a UE connected to a 5GC network using Standalone (SA) access. 33 
A2.3.1 Assumptions 34 
This example is based on the following design assumptions: 35 
1 Event trigger defined using Style 2 (Call Process Breakpoint), Type 3 (Mobility Management) and Id 1 36 
(handover Preparation) with the assumption that this breakpoint corresponds to the point of the UE call process 37 
code in a gNB where a handover decision is to be taken based on a received RRC Measurement  report. 38 

 
ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.01 
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
 282 
a. Event Trigger Definition IE RAN parameters for Associated E2 Node Info IE are not used 1 
b. Event Trigger Definition IE RAN parameters for Associated UE Info IE are used to offer filtering of UE 2 
between those subject to Policy handling and those to be handled using default parameters.  In this example 3 
RAN parameters for discrimination based on Slice and Group (aka SPID) are described.  4 
2 Policy defined using Style 3 (Connected Mobile Mobility), Policy Action ID 1 (Policy for Handover control)  5 
a. Policy Condition Definition IE RAN parameters used to map UE to an appropriate Policy Action.  In this 6 
example RAN parameters based on Serving Cell and Explicit UE List membership are described.   7 
b. Policy Action Definition IE parameters used to define a set of offsets (+positive, zero or -negative values) to 8 
be applied to default measurement thresholds to calculate policy modified threshold used during Handover 9 
decision prior to Handover execution. 10 
3 Depending upon the outcome of the decision the gNB either: 11 
a. Proceeds with handover execution using information obtained from the measurement report, stored UE 12 
context information and result of subsequent network transactions 13 
b. Ignores measurement report and continues any other required call processing  14

A.2.3.2 RIC Event Trigger Definition IE contents 4 
RIC Event Trigger Definition IE contains RAN Parameter lists for Associated E2 Node Info IE and Associated UE info 5 
IE.  In this example, only the Associated UE info IE is used where the set of target UEs for the event is defined by a 6 
given slice (SST=sst1, SD=sd1) and group (IRFSP=irfsp1) 7 
Additional sets of target UEs may be supported using the same RAN Parameter list with different target values for SST, 8 
SD and IRFSP.  These would be combined within the Associated E2 Node Info IE using the optional "Logical OR" flag 9 
(see section 9.3.26). 10

A.2.3.3 RIC Action Definition IE contents 3 
RIC Action Definition IE contains RAN Parameter lists for Policy Condition Definition IE and Policy Action Definition 4 
IE.   5 
In this example the Policy Condition Definition IE is used to define the set of target UEs that are to be assigned a given 6 
Policy Action Definition IE based on a given Serving Cell (nr-cgi1) and membership of a given Explicit UE List 7 
(HOList1).  The corresponding Policy Action Definition IE is used to set the measurement threshold offset for A3 RSRP 8 
measurement threshold (A3-rsrp-off1) 9 
Different values of NR-CGI and/or Explicit UE List ID may be used in each Policy condition in the Action Definition  10 
IE, each with a corresponding different Policy Action definition. 11
